<rate>5< /rate>< Text>
Pain Management is a challenging field of medicine. With Government and CDC ‚Äúguidelines‚Äù that are often in conflict with what would work best for the patient. There are many therapeutic modalities and therapies that can be used, often in conjunction with a wide variety of medications. On my first visit, I learned that IPM has a tightly controlled policy of what they will prescribe and the limits used as guidelines. Because of this, there were no surprises and I had clear expectations going in. Mareena Miller has an excellent ability to evaluate, assess and suggest the best path of treatment. She gives no false promises and sets real expectations for outcomes. Having had 45 surgeries and a MRSA infection in my spine, I needed someone who could give me a realistic idea of what they could accomplish. Mareena did exactly that-and in a caring and compassionate but realistic way. The staff has been professional and this office is very consistent in how things are managed. Years ago, I wanted to hear a 100% cure and being pain free was not only possible, but likely. Experience has taught me that after you break almost every long bone in a harsh and traumatic  way, that outcome is not a realistic possibility. Now, I prefer the simplicity of ‚Äúhere is what we expect to achieve, and we can hope for even better results but this is the most likely outcome of this procedure, surgery, device, etc.
Having experienced both the very best of pain management and possibly the worst, I have found a practice that meets my needs, gives me hope and yet keeps it real. I have never met the owner/operator physician here because the team of Doctors/Nurse Practitioners/Physicians Assistants all seem so competent and understand the philosophy of this practice I am quite content and confident that the level of care here is very excellent and consistent across the board. Mareena Miller is excellent and I will be here for many years to come.< /Text>

I'm so disappointed with my visit. I'm a former patient who had to leave Inland Pain because they stopped accepting IEHP patients back in 2015. So the .05mg I take occasionally due to my disability, disqualifies me from being treated there. My disabilities include chronic pain due to conditions that the judge in my case ruled me 100% disabled.

I feel that after reading my intake questionnaire, she had a negative preconceived idea about me, and as a LEGITIMATE pain management patient, that is our worse nightmare. <Review>Having never ridden a motorcycle before, I wanted to learn from the best.  After research and talking with others, I selected Pacific Motorcycle Training to get the job done.  They were very knowledgeable and had the students learn each module well before continuing on to the next.  They provided the motorcycles and had several available for us to select from.  The classroom gave us much needed information about being safe on the roadways, types of equipment and apparel to wear for safety and for being visible to other motorists, riding while under the influence and the penalties (both from law enforcement and your physical being) involved, and how to ride during inclement weather and road conditions.  The benefit is that by taking this course you bypass the DMV "riding" part for getting a M1 designation on your drivers license.  You'll still have to take the DMV test (there are two which you can select from) but the dreaded "lollypop" and "weave" part of the "riding" test are avoided completely.

I hugely endorse this class if you're a beginning motorcycle rider and you won't be disappointed.  PMT also offers an Intermediate and Advanced course using your own motorcycle once you've gained some road time and experience.  All in all, a huge WIN for me as the class gave me confidence to ride and the knowledge to help keep me out of trouble.<//Review>< Pictures>
None< /Pictures>

I had an appointment for 3pm on Wednesday June 14th 2017. I dropped off my company fleet vehicle for a 30k mile service. They said it would take a few hours. I never received a call, and they close at 6pm. They locked my car in their bay overnight, and when I finally got ahold of someone the next morning, I found out no service was done to my car. I received a call 20 min later, informing me my vehicle was done. I pick up my vehicle and park it. Today, I go out to my vehicle and have a completely flat rear tire. I call and immediately they get defensive and tell my they only rotated the tires (which is not completely true, as the psi on all 4 of my tires was different, which means they at least added air) and I must have picked something up on my drove home. Now I am here a third day in a row for basically an oil change. As a 24hr on call employee, this is just unacceptable. I was already told by my company to not bring my vehicle here again, but with the service I received here the last couple of days, I will not be bringing any of my personal vehicles here anymore. Which is unfortunate as there are not many places near me that provide a one stop shop for maintenance.

Edit: They just finished "fixing" my tire. Apparently the tire was leaking from its bead. They are charging fleet for a flat repair, even though I drove 28,500 miles with no issue on this tire, but the 3.5 miles I drove home from this place caused the issue. This place is a joke.< /Text>
<name>Ilja Prins< /name><userid>109158580888346624633<//userid></record></dataset><record>
<time>1504803796787</time><Pics>None< /Pics><Name>Charles Hernandez</Name><Rate>4</Rate><Gmap_id>0x808ff8b6208aabf3:0xb9ca83a1248573ed< /Gmap_id><userid>106233751769917575422< /userid><response>None<//response>< Review>
I came to this Firestone in January because I had a really bad puncture in my passenger front wheel. I ordered a set of Potenza S-04s from Sherrie (I think she's the manager there?) and she was pretty friendly to me at the time. I waited about an hour and a half for the service to be completed. On July 4th on my way back from work, I saw my tire pressure light had turned itself on. Once I got home and checked the pressure, it was down about 9 psi, so I just refilled it and assumed nothing of it. The morning of the following day, the tire was completely flat. I refilled it and sprayed soap/water around the tire assuming there was a puncture. The leak seemed to be coming from the valve stem. (I've only owned the tires for 5 months at this time). I went back to Firestone the same morning and discussed my problem with a guy named Dominic (really nice guy, I recommend you seek him out if he's working). After he came back from checking the tire with me, he was kind enough to vouch that tire itself didn't look like it was damaged. Sherrie was stern and stated, despite my disagreement and the fact she didn't personally check, it was deemed to be road hazard related (no real signs that it was nicked, scrapped, etc). I decided to pay the fee to replace the value and move on. Well, last night ANOTHER valve stem started leaking on the rear passenger tire (seriously?) I HIGHLY doubt this was road hazard related and it made me very mad about the first one (I guess the driver front and rear are bound to fail sooner or later). I went down to Les Schwab's and they didn't even charge me to replace the stem.... despite the fact I didn't even take my car there to get the tires worked on!! The wait time was relatively the same. What was the bonus of me visiting the competition? The tech who worked on my car asked if I was pulling my tire stem because there wasn't any signs that something hit the stem (maybe my cat has been pulling my stems when he's mad?)

Edit 2: I'm going to leave the majority of the original post because it's important to show my clarification. I went into Firestone again because the same tire (front passenger) that was worked on started leaking again. Sherrie was at the front desk and I told her of the situation. I decided to be more constructive by mentioning the tech who'd happen to work on my car the two times I've had this issue (his name won't be posted for privacy and potential harassment). She promptly tackled my problem and even apologized that I was charged for the last valve stem (honestly, I could have mis-remembered about mentioning it was the valve stem particularly last time because I can get flustered having to deal with these issues before work). She also refunded me the last charge from Dominic which she didn't have to do, but she felt personally inclined to make things right. When all is said and done, Firestone is a pretty awesome place when you're objective and cool-headed because Sherrie did take the time to hear me out when most corporations/chains simply don't and generally enforce policy. You might wanna catch her early in the morning though because after 9, I notice customers start coming in droves (I was there at 8 this morning I was still behind 3 people. Les Schwab's isn't different in that regard). When you're under that much pressure and a customer is being rude (like I most likely was before work that day) it's hard to be nice regardless of the situation. (I've done bookkeeping for an auto garage in the older part of Antioch and their customer's gave me headaches despite the fact I never had to deal with them).

When Firestone replaced the valve stem this time, they did see that the tech working on the tires wasn't properly installing it (maybe he didn't have experience on my particular model's rim size) and I'm sure he'll be taught so he doesn't repeat the problem! :D

I did remove an after-note I placed as well because it was rude and I shouldn't have done it. I also changed the second sentence because I bought a set, not two. A couple of grammatical fixes were made as well.</Review>

(Original)
SLOW AND DECEIVING TURNAROUND, DO NOT USE FOR SHORT TESTING WINDOWS

My appointment was about 52 hours before my flight, and the guy told me that most likely it would come back the next day, and if not, then definitely the day after. Well he lied, because when I asked about my test a few hours before my flight while it was STILL unprocessed, customer service told me that day of test AND Sundays don't count in their 1-2 day turnaround. So 1-2 days ended up being 4 for me, which doesn't even fit in the 72 hour window of testing required for my flight. Just get tested IN the airport, it is expensive but the turnaround was in minutes. Btw it's a "mid-turbinate" test which doesn't qualify for travel to Japan.
